# TechBuddy Three-Year Master Plan (36 Months)

Document type: Strategic and operational execution plan
Scope: Product, frontend, backend, design, accessibility, reachability, partnerships, operations, and governance
Planning horizon: 36 months (April 2026 to March 2029)
Audience: Product, engineering, design, operations, leadership, center instructors, and partners

## Purpose

TechBuddy exists to help senior citizens stay safe from scams, build smartphone confidence, and understand AI in plain language. This plan translates that purpose into a detailed, month-by-month operating system with concrete deliverables and measurable outcomes.

## Three-Year Goals

1. Build the most trusted senior-first digital safety and learning companion for community centers.
2. Reach sustainable multi-center adoption with measurable retention and task completion outcomes.
3. Deliver a reliable, secure, and accessible platform that remains calm and easy to use across mobile, tablet, and desktop.
4. Establish an evidence-backed impact model that demonstrates reduced scam susceptibility and improved digital confidence.
5. Build an operating model that can scale responsibly through partnerships, grants, and mission-aligned commercialization.

## Strategic Principles

1. Senior dignity first: every flow should reduce anxiety and increase confidence.
2. Accessibility by default: all releases must preserve readability, keyboard support, and assistive compatibility.
3. Safety over novelty: every AI feature must include guardrails, transparency, and fallback guidance.
4. Operational discipline: release quality and incident response are part of product quality.
5. Evidence over assumption: roadmap decisions require user research and measurable outcomes.

## Operating Cadence

1. Monthly execution plans with one-page briefs for every domain.
2. Quarterly reviews for priorities, risks, and budget alignment.
3. Biannual strategy refresh with partner and user advisory input.
4. Annual impact report with product, learning, and trust outcomes.

## Page Accounting

This document contains 360 one-page execution briefs:

1. 10 strategy domains per month.
2. 36 months of planning coverage.
3. Total one-page sections: 360.

Each section below is written as a standalone page brief.

## Page 001 | Year 1 Month 01 | Purpose and Impact

Planning window: Global month 1 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Trust and Baseline
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Define and validate the measurable impact model for senior confidence, scam safety, and independent task completion.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Publish monthly impact brief linking product changes to senior confidence and scam prevention outcomes.
2. Run structured interviews with seniors, caregivers, and center staff; convert findings into ranked roadmap decisions.
3. Maintain a mission alignment scorecard to ensure all releases support dignity, independence, and safety.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Monthly active senior learners and returning learner rate by device class
2. Scam-check comprehension score from post-interaction surveys
3. Phone-help completion rate and repeat usage within 30 days
4. Program progress checkpoint: 2 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: feature complexity grows faster than user comprehension. Mitigation: readability and simplicity review gates before release.
2. Risk: impact claims are weakly evidenced. Mitigation: quarterly evidence audits and external advisor review.

Definition of done: impact updates are published, reviewed, and tied to approved backlog changes.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 002 | Year 1 Month 01 | User Research and Reachability

Planning window: Global month 1 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Trust and Baseline
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Build a reliable research and outreach pipeline that reflects real senior behaviors and barriers.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Run monthly usability sessions with seniors across mobile, tablet, and desktop contexts.
2. Map high-friction journeys and produce prioritized fixes with clear owner and due date.
3. Operate an outreach calendar for family channels, center staff channels, and community partner channels.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. New user activation rate by acquisition source
2. First-session completion rate for one core journey
3. Percent of research findings closed within two quarters
4. Program progress checkpoint: 2 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: under-representation of older seniors and low-vision users. Mitigation: quota-based research recruiting.
2. Risk: outreach over-promises product capability. Mitigation: shared messaging review and claim governance.

Definition of done: research insights are synthesized, acted on, and reflected in next-quarter priorities.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 003 | Year 1 Month 01 | Frontend Experience and Design

Planning window: Global month 1 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Trust and Baseline
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Establish a calm, senior-first interface system with strong readability and predictable navigation.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Maintain component-level design tokens, spacing rhythm, and interaction standards for all primary routes.
2. Deliver monthly UI refinements that reduce confusion and improve task confidence on small screens.
3. Run visual QA and content readability pass before each release candidate.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Task success rate in Scam Checker, Phone Help, What Is AI, and Practice Mode
2. UI defect escape rate by severity
3. Median time to complete one guided task
4. Program progress checkpoint: 2 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: visual inconsistency increases cognitive load. Mitigation: mandatory design-system conformance checks.
2. Risk: interaction changes break learned behavior. Mitigation: incremental rollout with rollback criteria.

Definition of done: all new UI changes pass readability, consistency, and multi-device acceptance criteria.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 004 | Year 1 Month 01 | Accessibility and Inclusion

Planning window: Global month 1 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Trust and Baseline
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Institutionalize accessibility controls and audits as a non-negotiable release requirement.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Perform monthly accessibility audits covering keyboard flow, focus visibility, contrast, and semantics.
2. Expand readable content patterns, assistive support notes, and inclusive copy standards.
3. Track and resolve accessibility debt with explicit severity, owner, and completion dates.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Accessibility defect count by severity and route
2. Keyboard-only journey completion rate
3. Readability score and content complexity trend
4. Program progress checkpoint: 2 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: accessibility defects reappear in fast releases. Mitigation: CI gates and pre-merge checks.
2. Risk: language complexity drifts upward. Mitigation: editorial review with plain-language standards.

Definition of done: no high-severity accessibility regressions and all flagged issues have closure plans.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 005 | Year 1 Month 01 | Backend Platform and APIs

Planning window: Global month 1 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Trust and Baseline
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Stabilize backend route handlers, API contracts, and error-handling behavior across core flows.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Maintain versioned API contracts for scam analysis, AI chat, and practice endpoints.
2. Improve response consistency, fallback handling, and request tracing for all critical paths.
3. Run monthly backend review for dependency health, rate limiting posture, and operational bottlenecks.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. API success rate and p95 latency by route
2. Error class distribution and retry effectiveness
3. Rate-limit protection accuracy versus false blocking
4. Program progress checkpoint: 2 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: external model provider instability affects key flows. Mitigation: timeout policy and fallback messaging.
2. Risk: backend growth outpaces operational visibility. Mitigation: route-level telemetry and monthly architecture review.

Definition of done: API behavior is documented, monitored, and verified against reliability thresholds.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 006 | Year 1 Month 01 | AI Safety and Learning Quality

Planning window: Global month 1 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Trust and Baseline
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Ensure AI responses are clear, safe, and senior-appropriate in all supported journeys.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Maintain prompt governance with monthly review of unsafe, unclear, or overly technical outputs.
2. Run scenario-based evaluations for scam detection guidance, AI explanations, and roleplay feedback.
3. Publish quality notes that tie model behavior improvements to user trust outcomes.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Unsafe or confusing response incidence rate
2. Prompt adherence score for plain-language criteria
3. Scenario evaluation pass rate across high-risk scam patterns
4. Program progress checkpoint: 2 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: model drift introduces harmful advice tone. Mitigation: evaluation suite with release-blocking thresholds.
2. Risk: confidence language overstates certainty. Mitigation: response policy templates and editorial guardrails.

Definition of done: AI outputs meet clarity and safety thresholds with traceable evaluation evidence.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 007 | Year 1 Month 01 | Data, Privacy, and Compliance

Planning window: Global month 1 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Trust and Baseline
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Establish transparent and minimal data practices that support user trust and legal hygiene.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Review monthly data inventory for collection necessity, retention timelines, and access controls.
2. Maintain privacy notices and center-facing guidance in plain language.
3. Run quarterly compliance readiness checks aligned to evolving partnership requirements.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Data inventory completeness and owner coverage
2. Privacy issue count and remediation time
3. Retention policy conformance rate
4. Program progress checkpoint: 2 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: data scope expands without clear purpose. Mitigation: data-minimization review before feature approval.
2. Risk: unclear user disclosure language. Mitigation: legal-editorial dual review process.

Definition of done: privacy commitments are documented, traceable, and verifiably implemented.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 008 | Year 1 Month 01 | Reliability, Security, and Operations

Planning window: Global month 1 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Trust and Baseline
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Reach consistent release reliability with clear incident response and quality discipline.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Execute monthly reliability drills covering release rollback, incident triage, and communication handoff.
2. Track defect classes, test flakiness, and recovery times with corrective action ownership.
3. Review security posture for dependency risk, route abuse, and authentication boundaries.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Build and release success rate
2. Incident count by severity and mean time to recovery
3. Critical vulnerability remediation lead time
4. Program progress checkpoint: 2 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: hidden flaky tests mask regressions. Mitigation: flake budget and deterministic fix policy.
2. Risk: incident response drift across owners. Mitigation: runbook rehearsal and role clarity updates.

Definition of done: operational metrics improve or hold steady with completed corrective actions.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 009 | Year 1 Month 01 | Partnerships, Distribution, and Community Centers

Planning window: Global month 1 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Trust and Baseline
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Establish repeatable center adoption playbooks and trust-based onboarding materials.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Run monthly partner enablement sessions with center coordinators and instructors.
2. Maintain deployment kits with onboarding guides, classroom usage patterns, and escalation paths.
3. Track adoption quality, activation consistency, and retention by partner cohort.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Active partner centers and monthly retention
2. Center-level learner activation and repeat usage
3. Partner satisfaction and renewal intent indicators
4. Program progress checkpoint: 2 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: inconsistent center onboarding outcomes. Mitigation: standardized rollout checklist and mentor support.
2. Risk: distribution grows faster than support capacity. Mitigation: phased expansion with readiness gating.

Definition of done: partner outcomes are measured, reviewed, and fed back into rollout priorities.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 010 | Year 1 Month 01 | Team, Finance, and Governance

Planning window: Global month 1 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Trust and Baseline
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Build a disciplined team operating model with clear roles, budget controls, and decision rights.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Run monthly planning reviews for staffing capacity, budget utilization, and priority alignment.
2. Maintain decision logs for roadmap trade-offs, risk acceptance, and scope changes.
3. Track funding readiness milestones, partner obligations, and operating runway assumptions.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Planned versus actual milestone completion
2. Budget variance by quarter
3. Role coverage for critical product and operational functions
4. Program progress checkpoint: 2 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: unclear ownership slows delivery. Mitigation: role matrix review and escalation clarity.
2. Risk: budget pressure reduces quality. Mitigation: quality floor policy and staged scope controls.

Definition of done: team capacity, budget health, and governance records remain current and actionable.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 022 | Year 1 Month 03 | User Research and Reachability

Planning window: Global month 3 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Scam Resilience
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Build a reliable research and outreach pipeline that reflects real senior behaviors and barriers.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Run monthly usability sessions with seniors across mobile, tablet, and desktop contexts.
2. Map high-friction journeys and produce prioritized fixes with clear owner and due date.
3. Operate an outreach calendar for family channels, center staff channels, and community partner channels.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. New user activation rate by acquisition source
2. First-session completion rate for one core journey
3. Percent of research findings closed within two quarters
4. Program progress checkpoint: 8 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: under-representation of older seniors and low-vision users. Mitigation: quota-based research recruiting.
2. Risk: outreach over-promises product capability. Mitigation: shared messaging review and claim governance.

Definition of done: research insights are synthesized, acted on, and reflected in next-quarter priorities.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 023 | Year 1 Month 03 | Frontend Experience and Design

Planning window: Global month 3 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Scam Resilience
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Establish a calm, senior-first interface system with strong readability and predictable navigation.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Maintain component-level design tokens, spacing rhythm, and interaction standards for all primary routes.
2. Deliver monthly UI refinements that reduce confusion and improve task confidence on small screens.
3. Run visual QA and content readability pass before each release candidate.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Task success rate in Scam Checker, Phone Help, What Is AI, and Practice Mode
2. UI defect escape rate by severity
3. Median time to complete one guided task
4. Program progress checkpoint: 8 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: visual inconsistency increases cognitive load. Mitigation: mandatory design-system conformance checks.
2. Risk: interaction changes break learned behavior. Mitigation: incremental rollout with rollback criteria.

Definition of done: all new UI changes pass readability, consistency, and multi-device acceptance criteria.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 024 | Year 1 Month 03 | Accessibility and Inclusion

Planning window: Global month 3 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Scam Resilience
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Institutionalize accessibility controls and audits as a non-negotiable release requirement.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Perform monthly accessibility audits covering keyboard flow, focus visibility, contrast, and semantics.
2. Expand readable content patterns, assistive support notes, and inclusive copy standards.
3. Track and resolve accessibility debt with explicit severity, owner, and completion dates.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Accessibility defect count by severity and route
2. Keyboard-only journey completion rate
3. Readability score and content complexity trend
4. Program progress checkpoint: 8 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: accessibility defects reappear in fast releases. Mitigation: CI gates and pre-merge checks.
2. Risk: language complexity drifts upward. Mitigation: editorial review with plain-language standards.

Definition of done: no high-severity accessibility regressions and all flagged issues have closure plans.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

## Page 025 | Year 1 Month 03 | Backend Platform and APIs

Planning window: Global month 3 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Scam Resilience
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Stabilize backend route handlers, API contracts, and error-handling behavior across core flows.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Maintain versioned API contracts for scam analysis, AI chat, and practice endpoints.
2. Improve response consistency, fallback handling, and request tracing for all critical paths.
3. Run monthly backend review for dependency health, rate limiting posture, and operational bottlenecks.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. API success rate and p95 latency by route
2. Error class distribution and retry effectiveness
3. Rate-limit protection accuracy versus false blocking
4. Program progress checkpoint: 8 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: external model provider instability affects key flows. Mitigation: timeout policy and fallback messaging.
2. Risk: backend growth outpaces operational visibility. Mitigation: route-level telemetry and monthly architecture review.

Definition of done: API behavior is documented, monitored, and verified against reliability thresholds.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

## Page 026 | Year 1 Month 03 | AI Safety and Learning Quality

Planning window: Global month 3 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Scam Resilience
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Ensure AI responses are clear, safe, and senior-appropriate in all supported journeys.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Maintain prompt governance with monthly review of unsafe, unclear, or overly technical outputs.
2. Run scenario-based evaluations for scam detection guidance, AI explanations, and roleplay feedback.
3. Publish quality notes that tie model behavior improvements to user trust outcomes.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Unsafe or confusing response incidence rate
2. Prompt adherence score for plain-language criteria
3. Scenario evaluation pass rate across high-risk scam patterns
4. Program progress checkpoint: 8 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: model drift introduces harmful advice tone. Mitigation: evaluation suite with release-blocking thresholds.
2. Risk: confidence language overstates certainty. Mitigation: response policy templates and editorial guardrails.

Definition of done: AI outputs meet clarity and safety thresholds with traceable evaluation evidence.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

## Page 027 | Year 1 Month 03 | Data, Privacy, and Compliance

Planning window: Global month 3 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Scam Resilience
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Establish transparent and minimal data practices that support user trust and legal hygiene.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Review monthly data inventory for collection necessity, retention timelines, and access controls.
2. Maintain privacy notices and center-facing guidance in plain language.
3. Run quarterly compliance readiness checks aligned to evolving partnership requirements.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Data inventory completeness and owner coverage
2. Privacy issue count and remediation time
3. Retention policy conformance rate
4. Program progress checkpoint: 8 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: data scope expands without clear purpose. Mitigation: data-minimization review before feature approval.
2. Risk: unclear user disclosure language. Mitigation: legal-editorial dual review process.

Definition of done: privacy commitments are documented, traceable, and verifiably implemented.

## Page 028 | Year 1 Month 03 | Reliability, Security, and Operations

Planning window: Global month 3 of 36, Quarter 1
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Scam Resilience
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Reach consistent release reliability with clear incident response and quality discipline.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Execute monthly reliability drills covering release rollback, incident triage, and communication handoff.
2. Track defect classes, test flakiness, and recovery times with corrective action ownership.
3. Review security posture for dependency risk, route abuse, and authentication boundaries.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Build and release success rate
2. Incident count by severity and mean time to recovery
3. Critical vulnerability remediation lead time
4. Program progress checkpoint: 8 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: hidden flaky tests mask regressions. Mitigation: flake budget and deterministic fix policy.
2. Risk: incident response drift across owners. Mitigation: runbook rehearsal and role clarity updates.

Definition of done: operational metrics improve or hold steady with completed corrective actions.

## Page 031 | Year 1 Month 04 | Purpose and Impact

Planning window: Global month 4 of 36, Quarter 2
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Caregiver Confidence
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Define and validate the measurable impact model for senior confidence, scam safety, and independent task completion.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Publish monthly impact brief linking product changes to senior confidence and scam prevention outcomes.
2. Run structured interviews with seniors, caregivers, and center staff; convert findings into ranked roadmap decisions.
3. Maintain a mission alignment scorecard to ensure all releases support dignity, independence, and safety.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Monthly active senior learners and returning learner rate by device class
2. Scam-check comprehension score from post-interaction surveys
3. Phone-help completion rate and repeat usage within 30 days
4. Program progress checkpoint: 11 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: feature complexity grows faster than user comprehension. Mitigation: readability and simplicity review gates before release.
2. Risk: impact claims are weakly evidenced. Mitigation: quarterly evidence audits and external advisor review.

Definition of done: impact updates are published, reviewed, and tied to approved backlog changes.

Execution focus: Build and launch with staged validation.

Primary goal
Institutionalize accessibility controls and audits as a non-negotiable release requirement.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Perform monthly accessibility audits covering keyboard flow, focus visibility, contrast, and semantics.
2. Expand readable content patterns, assistive support notes, and inclusive copy standards.
3. Track and resolve accessibility debt with explicit severity, owner, and completion dates.
4. Deliver scoped changes, run pilot validation, and document rollout guidance.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Accessibility defect count by severity and route
2. Keyboard-only journey completion rate
3. Readability score and content complexity trend
4. Program progress checkpoint: 13 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: accessibility defects reappear in fast releases. Mitigation: CI gates and pre-merge checks.
2. Risk: language complexity drifts upward. Mitigation: editorial review with plain-language standards.

Definition of done: no high-severity accessibility regressions and all flagged issues have closure plans.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 045 | Year 1 Month 05 | Backend Platform and APIs

Planning window: Global month 5 of 36, Quarter 2
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Mobile and Tablet Mastery
Execution focus: Build and launch with staged validation.

Primary goal
Stabilize backend route handlers, API contracts, and error-handling behavior across core flows.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Maintain versioned API contracts for scam analysis, AI chat, and practice endpoints.
2. Improve response consistency, fallback handling, and request tracing for all critical paths.
3. Run monthly backend review for dependency health, rate limiting posture, and operational bottlenecks.
4. Deliver scoped changes, run pilot validation, and document rollout guidance.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. API success rate and p95 latency by route
2. Error class distribution and retry effectiveness
3. Rate-limit protection accuracy versus false blocking
4. Program progress checkpoint: 13 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: external model provider instability affects key flows. Mitigation: timeout policy and fallback messaging.
2. Risk: backend growth outpaces operational visibility. Mitigation: route-level telemetry and monthly architecture review.

Definition of done: API behavior is documented, monitored, and verified against reliability thresholds.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

## Page 046 | Year 1 Month 05 | AI Safety and Learning Quality

Planning window: Global month 5 of 36, Quarter 2
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Mobile and Tablet Mastery
Execution focus: Build and launch with staged validation.

Primary goal
Ensure AI responses are clear, safe, and senior-appropriate in all supported journeys.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Maintain prompt governance with monthly review of unsafe, unclear, or overly technical outputs.
2. Run scenario-based evaluations for scam detection guidance, AI explanations, and roleplay feedback.
3. Publish quality notes that tie model behavior improvements to user trust outcomes.
4. Deliver scoped changes, run pilot validation, and document rollout guidance.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Unsafe or confusing response incidence rate
2. Prompt adherence score for plain-language criteria
3. Scenario evaluation pass rate across high-risk scam patterns
4. Program progress checkpoint: 13 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: model drift introduces harmful advice tone. Mitigation: evaluation suite with release-blocking thresholds.
2. Risk: confidence language overstates certainty. Mitigation: response policy templates and editorial guardrails.

Definition of done: AI outputs meet clarity and safety thresholds with traceable evaluation evidence.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

## Page 047 | Year 1 Month 05 | Data, Privacy, and Compliance

Planning window: Global month 5 of 36, Quarter 2
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Mobile and Tablet Mastery
Execution focus: Build and launch with staged validation.

Primary goal
Establish transparent and minimal data practices that support user trust and legal hygiene.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Review monthly data inventory for collection necessity, retention timelines, and access controls.
2. Maintain privacy notices and center-facing guidance in plain language.
3. Run quarterly compliance readiness checks aligned to evolving partnership requirements.
4. Deliver scoped changes, run pilot validation, and document rollout guidance.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Data inventory completeness and owner coverage
2. Privacy issue count and remediation time
3. Retention policy conformance rate
4. Program progress checkpoint: 13 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: data scope expands without clear purpose. Mitigation: data-minimization review before feature approval.
2. Risk: unclear user disclosure language. Mitigation: legal-editorial dual review process.

Definition of done: privacy commitments are documented, traceable, and verifiably implemented.

## Page 048 | Year 1 Month 05 | Reliability, Security, and Operations

Planning window: Global month 5 of 36, Quarter 2
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Mobile and Tablet Mastery
Execution focus: Build and launch with staged validation.

Primary goal
Reach consistent release reliability with clear incident response and quality discipline.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Execute monthly reliability drills covering release rollback, incident triage, and communication handoff.
2. Track defect classes, test flakiness, and recovery times with corrective action ownership.
3. Review security posture for dependency risk, route abuse, and authentication boundaries.
4. Deliver scoped changes, run pilot validation, and document rollout guidance.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Build and release success rate
2. Incident count by severity and mean time to recovery
3. Critical vulnerability remediation lead time
4. Program progress checkpoint: 13 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: hidden flaky tests mask regressions. Mitigation: flake budget and deterministic fix policy.
2. Risk: incident response drift across owners. Mitigation: runbook rehearsal and role clarity updates.

Definition of done: operational metrics improve or hold steady with completed corrective actions.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

## Page 051 | Year 1 Month 06 | Purpose and Impact

Planning window: Global month 6 of 36, Quarter 2
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Instructor Enablement
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Define and validate the measurable impact model for senior confidence, scam safety, and independent task completion.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Publish monthly impact brief linking product changes to senior confidence and scam prevention outcomes.
2. Run structured interviews with seniors, caregivers, and center staff; convert findings into ranked roadmap decisions.
3. Maintain a mission alignment scorecard to ensure all releases support dignity, independence, and safety.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Monthly active senior learners and returning learner rate by device class
2. Scam-check comprehension score from post-interaction surveys
3. Phone-help completion rate and repeat usage within 30 days
4. Program progress checkpoint: 16 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: feature complexity grows faster than user comprehension. Mitigation: readability and simplicity review gates before release.
2. Risk: impact claims are weakly evidenced. Mitigation: quarterly evidence audits and external advisor review.

Definition of done: impact updates are published, reviewed, and tied to approved backlog changes.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

## Page 052 | Year 1 Month 06 | User Research and Reachability

Planning window: Global month 6 of 36, Quarter 2
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Instructor Enablement
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Build a reliable research and outreach pipeline that reflects real senior behaviors and barriers.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Run monthly usability sessions with seniors across mobile, tablet, and desktop contexts.
2. Map high-friction journeys and produce prioritized fixes with clear owner and due date.
3. Operate an outreach calendar for family channels, center staff channels, and community partner channels.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. New user activation rate by acquisition source
2. First-session completion rate for one core journey
3. Percent of research findings closed within two quarters
4. Program progress checkpoint: 16 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: under-representation of older seniors and low-vision users. Mitigation: quota-based research recruiting.
2. Risk: outreach over-promises product capability. Mitigation: shared messaging review and claim governance.

Definition of done: research insights are synthesized, acted on, and reflected in next-quarter priorities.

2. Run scenario-based evaluations for scam detection guidance, AI explanations, and roleplay feedback.
3. Publish quality notes that tie model behavior improvements to user trust outcomes.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Unsafe or confusing response incidence rate
2. Prompt adherence score for plain-language criteria
3. Scenario evaluation pass rate across high-risk scam patterns
4. Program progress checkpoint: 19 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: model drift introduces harmful advice tone. Mitigation: evaluation suite with release-blocking thresholds.
2. Risk: confidence language overstates certainty. Mitigation: response policy templates and editorial guardrails.

Definition of done: AI outputs meet clarity and safety thresholds with traceable evaluation evidence.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

## Page 067 | Year 1 Month 07 | Data, Privacy, and Compliance

Planning window: Global month 7 of 36, Quarter 3
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: AI Literacy Depth
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal
Establish transparent and minimal data practices that support user trust and legal hygiene.

2. Privacy issue count and remediation time
3. Retention policy conformance rate
4. Program progress checkpoint: 19 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: data scope expands without clear purpose. Mitigation: data-minimization review before feature approval.
2. Risk: unclear user disclosure language. Mitigation: legal-editorial dual review process.

Definition of done: privacy commitments are documented, traceable, and verifiably implemented.

## Page 068 | Year 1 Month 07 | Reliability, Security, and Operations

Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: AI Literacy Depth
Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

Primary goal

Concrete outcomes for this month

2. Track defect classes, test flakiness, and recovery times with corrective action ownership.
3. Review security posture for dependency risk, route abuse, and authentication boundaries.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Build and release success rate
2. Incident count by severity and mean time to recovery
3. Critical vulnerability remediation lead time
4. Program progress checkpoint: 19 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: hidden flaky tests mask regressions. Mitigation: flake budget and deterministic fix policy.
2. Risk: incident response drift across owners. Mitigation: runbook rehearsal and role clarity updates.

Definition of done: operational metrics improve or hold steady with completed corrective actions.

## Page 071 | Year 1 Month 08 | Purpose and Impact

Planning window: Global month 8 of 36, Quarter 3
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Operational Reliability
Execution focus: Build and launch with staged validation.

Primary goal
Define and validate the measurable impact model for senior confidence, scam safety, and independent task completion.

Concrete outcomes for this month

2. Run structured interviews with seniors, caregivers, and center staff; convert findings into ranked roadmap decisions.
3. Maintain a mission alignment scorecard to ensure all releases support dignity, independence, and safety.
4. Deliver scoped changes, run pilot validation, and document rollout guidance.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Monthly active senior learners and returning learner rate by device class
2. Scam-check comprehension score from post-interaction surveys
3. Phone-help completion rate and repeat usage within 30 days
4. Program progress checkpoint: 22 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: feature complexity grows faster than user comprehension. Mitigation: readability and simplicity review gates before release.
2. Risk: impact claims are weakly evidenced. Mitigation: quarterly evidence audits and external advisor review.

Definition of done: impact updates are published, reviewed, and tied to approved backlog changes.

## Page 072 | Year 1 Month 08 | User Research and Reachability

Planning window: Global month 8 of 36, Quarter 3
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Operational Reliability
Execution focus: Build and launch with staged validation.

3. Operate an outreach calendar for family channels, center staff channels, and community partner channels.
4. Deliver scoped changes, run pilot validation, and document rollout guidance.

3. Percent of research findings closed within two quarters

2. Risk: outreach over-promises product capability. Mitigation: shared messaging review and claim governance.

Definition of done: research insights are synthesized, acted on, and reflected in next-quarter priorities.

Definition of done: all new UI changes pass readability, consistency, and multi-device acceptance criteria.

Definition of done: API behavior is documented, monitored, and verified against reliability thresholds.

3. Critical vulnerability remediation lead time
4. Program progress checkpoint: 25 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: hidden flaky tests mask regressions. Mitigation: flake budget and deterministic fix policy.
2. Risk: incident response drift across owners. Mitigation: runbook rehearsal and role clarity updates.

Definition of done: operational metrics improve or hold steady with completed corrective actions.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

## Page 089 | Year 1 Month 09 | Partnerships, Distribution, and Community Centers

Planning window: Global month 9 of 36, Quarter 3
Program phase: Year 1: Foundation and Trust
Monthly theme: Community Reach
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal

2. Maintain deployment kits with onboarding guides, classroom usage patterns, and escalation paths.

2. Center-level learner activation and repeat usage
3. Partner satisfaction and renewal intent indicators
4. Program progress checkpoint: 25 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now

2. Risk: distribution grows faster than support capacity. Mitigation: phased expansion with readiness gating.

Definition of done: partner outcomes are measured, reviewed, and fed back into rollout priorities.

Execution focus: Discovery and planning with explicit acceptance criteria.

4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month

2. Scam-check comprehension score from post-interaction surveys
3. Phone-help completion rate and repeat usage within 30 days
4. Program progress checkpoint: 27 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: feature complexity grows faster than user comprehension. Mitigation: readability and simplicity review gates before release.
2. Risk: impact claims are weakly evidenced. Mitigation: quarterly evidence audits and external advisor review.

Definition of done: impact updates are published, reviewed, and tied to approved backlog changes.

Definition of done: research insights are synthesized, acted on, and reflected in next-quarter priorities.

Monthly theme: Language and Inclusion Expansion

Dependencies and risks to manage now

2. Risk: language complexity drifts upward. Mitigation: editorial review with plain-language standards.

Definition of done: no high-severity accessibility regressions and all flagged issues have closure plans.

4. Program progress checkpoint: 27 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.

Dependencies and risks to manage now

2. Risk: backend growth outpaces operational visibility. Mitigation: route-level telemetry and monthly architecture review.

Definition of done: API behavior is documented, monitored, and verified against reliability thresholds.

4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Monthly active senior learners and returning learner rate by device class
2. Scam-check comprehension score from post-interaction surveys
3. Phone-help completion rate and repeat usage within 30 days
4. Program progress checkpoint: 33 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 85 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: feature complexity grows faster than user comprehension. Mitigation: readability and simplicity review gates before release.
2. Risk: impact claims are weakly evidenced. Mitigation: quarterly evidence audits and external advisor review.

Definition of done: impact updates are published, reviewed, and tied to approved backlog changes.

Scale design consistency and speed across all routes and feature expansions.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Maintain component-level design tokens, spacing rhythm, and interaction standards for all primary routes.
2. Deliver monthly UI refinements that reduce confusion and improve task confidence on small screens.
3. Run visual QA and content readability pass before each release candidate.
4. Deliver scoped changes, run pilot validation, and document rollout guidance.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Task success rate in Scam Checker, Phone Help, What Is AI, and Practice Mode
2. UI defect escape rate by severity
3. Median time to complete one guided task
4. Program progress checkpoint: 38 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 90 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: visual inconsistency increases cognitive load. Mitigation: mandatory design-system conformance checks.
2. Risk: interaction changes break learned behavior. Mitigation: incremental rollout with rollback criteria.

Definition of done: all new UI changes pass readability, consistency, and multi-device acceptance criteria.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

## Page 134 | Year 2 Month 02 | Accessibility and Inclusion

Planning window: Global month 14 of 36, Quarter 5
Program phase: Year 2: Scale and Standardization
Monthly theme: Usability Proof
Execution focus: Build and launch with staged validation.

Primary goal
Advance from baseline compliance to proactive inclusion for broader age and ability needs.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Perform monthly accessibility audits covering keyboard flow, focus visibility, contrast, and semantics.
2. Expand readable content patterns, assistive support notes, and inclusive copy standards.
3. Track and resolve accessibility debt with explicit severity, owner, and completion dates.
4. Deliver scoped changes, run pilot validation, and document rollout guidance.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Accessibility defect count by severity and route
2. Keyboard-only journey completion rate
3. Readability score and content complexity trend
4. Program progress checkpoint: 38 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 90 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: accessibility defects reappear in fast releases. Mitigation: CI gates and pre-merge checks.
2. Risk: language complexity drifts upward. Mitigation: editorial review with plain-language standards.

Definition of done: no high-severity accessibility regressions and all flagged issues have closure plans.

4. Program progress checkpoint: 38 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.

Dependencies and risks to manage now

2. Risk: backend growth outpaces operational visibility. Mitigation: route-level telemetry and monthly architecture review.

Definition of done: API behavior is documented, monitored, and verified against reliability thresholds.

3. Critical vulnerability remediation lead time
4. Program progress checkpoint: 38 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 90 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now

2. Risk: incident response drift across owners. Mitigation: runbook rehearsal and role clarity updates.

Definition of done: operational metrics improve or hold steady with completed corrective actions.

2. Risk: impact claims are weakly evidenced. Mitigation: quarterly evidence audits and external advisor review.

Definition of done: impact updates are published, reviewed, and tied to approved backlog changes.

2. Error class distribution and retry effectiveness
3. Rate-limit protection accuracy versus false blocking
4. Program progress checkpoint: 44 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 90 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: external model provider instability affects key flows. Mitigation: timeout policy and fallback messaging.
2. Risk: backend growth outpaces operational visibility. Mitigation: route-level telemetry and monthly architecture review.

Definition of done: API behavior is documented, monitored, and verified against reliability thresholds.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

Definition of done: AI outputs meet clarity and safety thresholds with traceable evaluation evidence.

## Page 178 | Year 2 Month 06 | Reliability, Security, and Operations

Planning window: Global month 18 of 36, Quarter 6
Program phase: Year 2: Scale and Standardization
Monthly theme: Instructor Enablement
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Improve operational efficiency through automation, faster triage, and stronger resilience patterns.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Execute monthly reliability drills covering release rollback, incident triage, and communication handoff.
2. Track defect classes, test flakiness, and recovery times with corrective action ownership.
3. Review security posture for dependency risk, route abuse, and authentication boundaries.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Build and release success rate
2. Incident count by severity and mean time to recovery
3. Critical vulnerability remediation lead time
4. Program progress checkpoint: 50 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 90 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: hidden flaky tests mask regressions. Mitigation: flake budget and deterministic fix policy.
2. Risk: incident response drift across owners. Mitigation: runbook rehearsal and role clarity updates.

Definition of done: operational metrics improve or hold steady with completed corrective actions.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

4. Program progress checkpoint: 52 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.

Dependencies and risks to manage now

2. Risk: impact claims are weakly evidenced. Mitigation: quarterly evidence audits and external advisor review.

Definition of done: impact updates are published, reviewed, and tied to approved backlog changes.

1. Run monthly planning reviews for staffing capacity, budget utilization, and priority alignment.
2. Maintain decision logs for roadmap trade-offs, risk acceptance, and scope changes.
3. Track funding readiness milestones, partner obligations, and operating runway assumptions.
4. Deliver scoped changes, run pilot validation, and document rollout guidance.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Planned versus actual milestone completion
2. Budget variance by quarter
3. Role coverage for critical product and operational functions
4. Program progress checkpoint: 55 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 90 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: unclear ownership slows delivery. Mitigation: role matrix review and escalation clarity.
2. Risk: budget pressure reduces quality. Mitigation: quality floor policy and staged scope controls.

Definition of done: team capacity, budget health, and governance records remain current and actionable.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

Planning window: Global month 21 of 36, Quarter 7
Program phase: Year 2: Scale and Standardization
Monthly theme: Community Reach
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

4. Program progress checkpoint: 58 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.

Dependencies and risks to manage now

2. Risk: impact claims are weakly evidenced. Mitigation: quarterly evidence audits and external advisor review.

Definition of done: impact updates are published, reviewed, and tied to approved backlog changes.

4. Program progress checkpoint: 63 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 90 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: under-representation of older seniors and low-vision users. Mitigation: quota-based research recruiting.
2. Risk: outreach over-promises product capability. Mitigation: shared messaging review and claim governance.

Definition of done: research insights are synthesized, acted on, and reflected in next-quarter priorities.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

Monthly theme: Evidence and Outcomes

4. Program progress checkpoint: 63 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.

Dependencies and risks to manage now

2. Risk: interaction changes break learned behavior. Mitigation: incremental rollout with rollback criteria.

Definition of done: all new UI changes pass readability, consistency, and multi-device acceptance criteria.

Monthly theme: Scam Resilience
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Maintain auditable privacy maturity suitable for institutional adoption and partner reviews.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Review monthly data inventory for collection necessity, retention timelines, and access controls.
2. Maintain privacy notices and center-facing guidance in plain language.
3. Run quarterly compliance readiness checks aligned to evolving partnership requirements.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Data inventory completeness and owner coverage
2. Privacy issue count and remediation time
3. Retention policy conformance rate
4. Program progress checkpoint: 75 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 92 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: data scope expands without clear purpose. Mitigation: data-minimization review before feature approval.
2. Risk: unclear user disclosure language. Mitigation: legal-editorial dual review process.

Definition of done: privacy commitments are documented, traceable, and verifiably implemented.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

## Page 268 | Year 3 Month 03 | Reliability, Security, and Operations

Planning window: Global month 27 of 36, Quarter 9
Program phase: Year 3: Expansion and Sustainability
Monthly theme: Scam Resilience
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Sustain enterprise-grade reliability habits suitable for larger partner expectations.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Execute monthly reliability drills covering release rollback, incident triage, and communication handoff.
2. Track defect classes, test flakiness, and recovery times with corrective action ownership.
3. Review security posture for dependency risk, route abuse, and authentication boundaries.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Build and release success rate
2. Incident count by severity and mean time to recovery
3. Critical vulnerability remediation lead time
4. Program progress checkpoint: 75 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 92 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: hidden flaky tests mask regressions. Mitigation: flake budget and deterministic fix policy.
2. Risk: incident response drift across owners. Mitigation: runbook rehearsal and role clarity updates.

Definition of done: operational metrics improve or hold steady with completed corrective actions.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

3. Maintain a mission alignment scorecard to ensure all releases support dignity, independence, and safety.
4. Complete design and planning artifacts, owner assignments, and dependency validation.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Monthly active senior learners and returning learner rate by device class
2. Scam-check comprehension score from post-interaction surveys
3. Phone-help completion rate and repeat usage within 30 days
4. Program progress checkpoint: 77 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 92 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: feature complexity grows faster than user comprehension. Mitigation: readability and simplicity review gates before release.
2. Risk: impact claims are weakly evidenced. Mitigation: quarterly evidence audits and external advisor review.

Definition of done: impact updates are published, reviewed, and tied to approved backlog changes.

3. Track adoption quality, activation consistency, and retention by partner cohort.
4. Deliver scoped changes, run pilot validation, and document rollout guidance.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Active partner centers and monthly retention
2. Center-level learner activation and repeat usage
3. Partner satisfaction and renewal intent indicators
4. Program progress checkpoint: 80 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 92 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: inconsistent center onboarding outcomes. Mitigation: standardized rollout checklist and mentor support.
2. Risk: distribution grows faster than support capacity. Mitigation: phased expansion with readiness gating.

Definition of done: partner outcomes are measured, reviewed, and fed back into rollout priorities.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

2. Scam-check comprehension score from post-interaction surveys
3. Phone-help completion rate and repeat usage within 30 days
4. Program progress checkpoint: 88 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 92 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: feature complexity grows faster than user comprehension. Mitigation: readability and simplicity review gates before release.
2. Risk: impact claims are weakly evidenced. Mitigation: quarterly evidence audits and external advisor review.

Definition of done: impact updates are published, reviewed, and tied to approved backlog changes.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

Definition of done: operational metrics improve or hold steady with completed corrective actions.

5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 92 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: visual inconsistency increases cognitive load. Mitigation: mandatory design-system conformance checks.
2. Risk: interaction changes break learned behavior. Mitigation: incremental rollout with rollback criteria.

Definition of done: all new UI changes pass readability, consistency, and multi-device acceptance criteria.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

One-page brief note: this section is intended to be treated as a standalone execution page in the printed plan set.

\pagebreak

## Page 356 | Year 3 Month 12 | AI Safety and Learning Quality

Planning window: Global month 36 of 36, Quarter 12
Program phase: Year 3: Expansion and Sustainability
Monthly theme: Planning and Renewal
Execution focus: Measure, optimize, and close the loop.

Primary goal
Operate a mature AI governance system with transparent quality and risk reporting.

Concrete outcomes for this month
1. Maintain prompt governance with monthly review of unsafe, unclear, or overly technical outputs.
2. Run scenario-based evaluations for scam detection guidance, AI explanations, and roleplay feedback.
3. Publish quality notes that tie model behavior improvements to user trust outcomes.
4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month
1. Unsafe or confusing response incidence rate
2. Prompt adherence score for plain-language criteria
3. Scenario evaluation pass rate across high-risk scam patterns
4. Program progress checkpoint: 100 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.
5. Monthly target gate: maintain at least 92 percent completion on committed milestones.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: model drift introduces harmful advice tone. Mitigation: evaluation suite with release-blocking thresholds.
2. Risk: confidence language overstates certainty. Mitigation: response policy templates and editorial guardrails.

Definition of done: AI outputs meet clarity and safety thresholds with traceable evaluation evidence.

Planning window: Global month 36 of 36, Quarter 12

4. Evaluate outcomes, resolve defects, and formalize next-quarter backlog updates.

Measures of success tracked this month

3. Critical vulnerability remediation lead time
4. Program progress checkpoint: 100 percent of three-year timeline elapsed.

Dependencies and risks to manage now
1. Risk: hidden flaky tests mask regressions. Mitigation: flake budget and deterministic fix policy.
2. Risk: incident response drift across owners. Mitigation: runbook rehearsal and role clarity updates.

Definition of done: operational metrics improve or hold steady with completed corrective actions.

## Closing Notes

The 360 page briefs above define a month-by-month execution framework for the next three years. Teams should use each page as a living operational brief, update assumptions quarterly, and preserve the mission of calm, trusted senior support in every release decision.
